       </a>
       . For the type of primate, see
       <a href="/wiki/Galago" title="Galago">
        Galago

        Galicia (Eastern Europe)
       </a>

       </a>

       <b>
        Galician
       </b>
       (
       <span class="nowrap">
        <span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt">
         <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">
          /
          <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted">
           <span title="/ɡ/: 'g' in 'guy'">
            ɡ
           </span>
           <span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">
            ə
           </span>
           <span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">
            ˈ
           </span>
           <span title="'l' in 'lie'">
            l
           </span>
           <span title="/ɪ/: 'i' in 'kit'">
            ɪ
           </span>
           <span title="/ʃ/: 'sh' in 'shy'">
            ʃ
           </span>
           <span title="/ən/: 'on' in 'button'">
            ən
           </span>
          </span>
          /
         </a>
        </span>
       </span>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5">
        <a href="#cite_note-5">
         [5]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <span class="nowrap">
        <span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt">
         <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">
          /-
          <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted">
           <span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">
            ˈ
           </span>
           <span title="'l' in 'lie'">
            l
           </span>
           <span title="/ɪ/: 'i' in 'kit'">
            ɪ
           </span>
           <span title="'s' in 'sigh'">
            s
           </span>
           <span title="/i/: 'y' in 'happy'">
            i
           </span>
           <span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">
            ə
           </span>
           <span title="'n' in 'nigh'">
            n
           </span>
          </span>
          /
         </a>
        </span>
       </span>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6">
        <a href="#cite_note-6">
         [6]
        </a>
       </sup>
       ;
       <i>
        <span lang="gl">
         <i>
          galego
         </i>
        </span>
       </i>
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Galician" title="Help:IPA/Galician">
         [ɡaˈleɣʊ]
        </a>
       </span>
       ) is an
       <a href="/wiki/Indo-European_languages" title="Indo-European languages">
        Indo-European language
       </a>
       of the
       <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Romance_languages" title="Iberian Romance languages">
        Western Ibero-Romance
       </a>
       branch. It is spoken by some 2.4 million people, mainly in
       <a href="/wiki/Galicia_(Spain)" title="Galicia (Spain)">
        Galicia
       </a>
       , an
       <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_communities_of_Spain" title="Autonomous communities of Spain">
        autonomous community
       </a>
       located in northwestern Spain, where it is official along with Spanish. The language is also spoken in some border zones of the neighbouring Spanish regions of
       <a href="/wiki/Asturias" title="Asturias">
        Asturias
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Castile_and_Le%C3%B3n" title="Castile and León">
        Castile and León
       </a>
       , as well as by Galician migrant communities in the rest of Spain, in Latin America, the United States,
       <a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">
        Switzerland
       </a>
       and elsewhere in Europe.
      </p>
      <p>
       Modern Galician is part of the
       <a href="/wiki/West_Iberian_languages" title="West Iberian languages">
        West Iberian languages
       </a>
       group, a family of
       <a href="/wiki/Romance_languages" title="Romance languages">
        Romance languages
       </a>
       that includes the
       <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">
        Portuguese language
       </a>
       , which developed locally from
       <a href="/wiki/Vulgar_Latin" title="Vulgar Latin">
        Vulgar Latin
       </a>
       and evolved into what modern scholars have called
       <a href="/wiki/Galician-Portuguese" title="Galician-Portuguese">
        Galician-Portuguese
       </a>
       . Dialectal divergences are observable between the northern and southern forms of Galician-Portuguese in 13th-century texts but the two dialects were similar enough to maintain a high level of cultural unity until the middle of the 14th century, producing the medieval
       <a href="/wiki/Galician-Portuguese_lyric" title="Galician-Portuguese lyric">
        Galician-Portuguese lyric
       </a>
       . The divergence has continued to this day, producing the modern languages of Galician and Portuguese.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7">
        <a href="#cite_note-7">
         [7]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Lexicon" title="Lexicon">
        lexicon
       </a>
       of Galician is predominantly of
       <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">
        Latin
       </a>
       extraction, although it also contains a moderate number of words of
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_Galician_words_of_Germanic_origin" title="List of Galician words of Germanic origin">
        Germanic
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_Galician_words_of_Celtic_origin" title="List of Galician words of Celtic origin">
        Celtic
       </a>
       origin, among other
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Substratum_(linguistics)" title="Substratum (linguistics)">
        substrates
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Adstrate" title="Adstrate">
        adstrates
       </a>
       , having also received, mainly via Spanish, a number of nouns from the Arabic of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Al_Andalus" title="Al Andalus">
        Al Andalus
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       The language is officially regulated in Galicia by the
       <a href="/wiki/Royal_Galician_Academy" title="Royal Galician Academy">
        Royal Galician Academy
       </a>
       . However, independent organisations, such as the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Galician_Association_of_Language" title="Galician Association of Language">
        Galician Association of Language
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Galician_Academy_of_the_Portuguese_Language" title="Galician Academy of the Portuguese Language">
        Galician Academy of the Portuguese Language
       </a>
       , include Galician as part of the Portuguese language, as the
       <a href="/wiki/Galician-Portuguese" title="Galician-Portuguese">
        Galician-Portuguese
       </a>
       variant.
      </p>
      <p>
      </p>

      <p>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Classification_and_relation_with_Portuguese">
        Classification and relation with Portuguese
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Galician_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Classification and relation with Portuguese">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Linguistic_map_Southwestern_Europe.gif">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="544" data-file-width="600" height="199" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Linguistic_map_Southwestern_Europe.gif/220px-Linguistic_map_Southwestern_Europe.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Linguistic_map_Southwestern_Europe.gif/330px-Linguistic_map_Southwestern_Europe.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Linguistic_map_Southwestern_Europe.gif/440px-Linguistic_map_Southwestern_Europe.gif 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Linguistic_map_Southwestern_Europe.gif" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Map showing the historical retreat and expansion of Galician (Galician and Portuguese) within the context of its linguistic neighbours between the year 1000 and 2000
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Modern Galician and its sibling,
       <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">
        Portuguese
       </a>
       , originated from a common medieval ancestor designated variously by modern linguists as Galician-Portuguese (Mediaeval Galician, Medieval Portuguese, Old Galician or Old Portuguese). This common ancestral stage developed in the territories of the old
       <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Galicia" title="Kingdom of Galicia">
        Kingdom of Galicia
       </a>
       , which covered the territories of modern-day Galicia and northern Portugal. In the 13th century it became a written and cultivated language.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8">
        <a href="#cite_note-8">
         [8]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In the past Galician and Portuguese formed a
       <a href="/wiki/Dialect_continuum" title="Dialect continuum">
        dialect continuum
       </a>
       . For many scholars this continuum still exists today at the level of rural dialects.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-instituto-camoes1971_9-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-instituto-camoes1971-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10">
        <a href="#cite_note-10">
         [10]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">
        <a href="#cite_note-11">
         [11]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Others point out that modern Galician and Portuguese have diverged to such an extent during the past seven centuries that they now constitute two closely related but separate languages.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">
        <a href="#cite_note-12">
         [12]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Historically, the Galician-Portuguese language originated from
       <a href="/wiki/Vulgar_Latin" title="Vulgar Latin">
        Vulgar Latin
       </a>
       as a Western
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Romance_language" title="Romance language">
        Romance language
       </a>
       in the lands now in Galicia, Asturias and northern half of
       <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">
        Portugal
       </a>
       , which belonged to the mediaeval Kingdom of Galicia, itself comprising approximately the former Roman territory of
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Gallaecia" title="Gallaecia">
         Gallaecia
        </a>
       </i>
       as modified during the two centuries of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Suevic_Kingdom_of_Galicia" title="Suevic Kingdom of Galicia">
        Suevic Kingdom of Galicia
       </a>
       . The standards of the language began to diverge in the 14th century, as Portuguese became the official language of the independent
       <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Portugal" title="Kingdom of Portugal">
        kingdom of Portugal
       </a>
       and its chancellery, while Galician was the language of the scriptoria of the lawyers, noblemen and churchmen of the Kingdom of Galicia, then integrated in the
       <a href="/wiki/Crown_of_Castile" title="Crown of Castile">
        crown of Castile
       </a>
       and open to influence from Castilian language, culture, and politics. During the 16th century the Galician language stopped being used in legal documentation, becoming de facto an oral language, with just some use in lyric, theatre and private letters.
      </p>
      <p>
       The linguistic status of Galician with respect to Portuguese is controversial, and the issue sometimes carries political overtones. There are
       <a href="/wiki/Linguistics" title="Linguistics">
        linguists
       </a>
       who deal with modern Galician and modern Portuguese as
       <a href="/wiki/Standard_language" title="Standard language">
        norms
       </a>
       or varieties of the same language.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">
        <a href="#cite_note-13">
         [13]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Some authors, such as
       <a href="/wiki/Lu%C3%ADs_Lindley_Cintra" title="Luís Lindley Cintra">
        Lindley Cintra
       </a>
       , consider that they are still co-dialects of a common language, in spite of superficial differences in phonology and vocabulary, while others, such as Pilar Vázquez Cuesta, argue that they have become separate languages due to major differences in phonetics and vocabulary usage, and, to a lesser extent, morphology and syntax.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-instituto-camoes1971_9-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-instituto-camoes1971-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">
        <a href="#cite_note-14">
         [14]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Fernández Rei in 1990 stated that the Galician language is, with respect to Portuguese, an
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ausbausprache,_Abstandsprache_and_Dachsprache" title="Ausbausprache, Abstandsprache and Dachsprache">
        <i>
         ausbau
        </i>
        language
       </a>
       , a language through elaboration, and not an
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ausbausprache,_Abstandsprache_and_Dachsprache" title="Ausbausprache, Abstandsprache and Dachsprache">
        <i>
         abstand
        </i>
        language
       </a>
       , a language through detachment.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15">
        <a href="#cite_note-15">
         [15]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       With respect to the external and internal perception of this relation, for instance in past editions of the
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Encyclop%C3%A6dia_Britannica" title="Encyclopædia Britannica">
         Encyclopædia Britannica
        </a>
       </i>
       , Galician was defined as a
       <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_dialects" title="Portuguese dialects">
        Portuguese dialect
       </a>
       spoken in northwestern Spain. However, most Galician speakers do not regard Galician as a variety of Portuguese, but as a different language,
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2016)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       as modern Galician evolved without interruption and in situ from Mediaeval Galician-Portuguese.
      </p>
      <p>
       Mutual intelligibility (estimated at 85% by
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Robert_A._Hall,_Jr." title="Robert A. Hall, Jr.">
        Robert A. Hall, Jr.
       </a>
       , 1989) is very high between Galicians and Portuguese.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-e18_1-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-e18-1">
         [1]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       On 20 October 2016, the city of
       <a href="/wiki/Santiago_de_Compostela" title="Santiago de Compostela">
        Santiago de Compostela
       </a>
       , the capital of
       <a href="/wiki/Galicia_(Spain)" title="Galicia (Spain)">
        Galicia
       </a>
       , approved by unanimity a proposal to become an observer member of the Union of Portuguese-Speaking Capitals (UCCLA).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16">
        <a href="#cite_note-16">
         [16]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       On 1 November 2016, the Council of Galician Culture (Consello da Cultura Galega) was admitted as a consultative observer of the
       <a href="/wiki/Community_of_Portuguese_Language_Countries" title="Community of Portuguese Language Countries">
        Community of Portuguese Speaking Countries
       </a>
       (CPLP).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">
        <a href="#cite_note-17">
         [17]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Opposing_views">
        Opposing views
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Galician_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Opposing views">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Martim_Codax_Cantigas_de_Amigo.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1130" data-file-width="1559" height="159" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Martim_Codax_Cantigas_de_Amigo.jpg/220px-Martim_Codax_Cantigas_de_Amigo.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Martim_Codax_Cantigas_de_Amigo.jpg/330px-Martim_Codax_Cantigas_de_Amigo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Martim_Codax_Cantigas_de_Amigo.jpg/440px-Martim_Codax_Cantigas_de_Amigo.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Martim_Codax_Cantigas_de_Amigo.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Vindel's parchment, containing music and lyrics of several 13th-century
         <i>
          cantigas
         </i>
         by
         <a href="/wiki/Martin_Codax" title="Martin Codax">
          Martin Codax
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The official position of the Galician Language Institute is that Galician and Portuguese should be considered independent languages.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2011)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       The standard
       <a href="/wiki/Orthography" title="Orthography">
        orthography
       </a>
       is noticeably different from that of Portuguese, partly because of divergent phonological features, and partly due to the use of Spanish (Castilian) orthographic conventions, which ignore many proper Galician features, like open and close vowels, which do not exist in Spanish.
      </p>
      <p>
       The official institution regulating the Galician language, backed by the Galician government and universities, the
       <a href="/wiki/Royal_Galician_Academy" title="Royal Galician Academy">
        Royal Galician Academy
       </a>
       , claims that modern Galician must be considered an independent
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Romance_language" title="Romance language">
        Romance language
       </a>
       belonging to the group of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ibero-Romance" title="Ibero-Romance">
        Ibero-Romance
       </a>
       languages and having strong ties with Portuguese and its northern dialects.
      </p>
      <p>
       However, the
       <a href="/wiki/Galician_Language_Association" title="Galician Language Association">
        Galician Language Association
       </a>
       (
       <i>
        Associaçom Galega da Língua
       </i>
       ) and
       <a href="/wiki/Galician_Academy_of_the_Portuguese_Language" title="Galician Academy of the Portuguese Language">
        Galician Academy of the Portuguese Language
       </a>
       (
       <i>
        Academia Galega da Língua Portuguesa
       </i>
       ), belonging to the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Reintegrationist" title="Reintegrationist">
        Reintegrationist
       </a>
       movement, support the idea that differences between Galician and Portuguese speech are not enough to justify considering them as separate languages: Galician is simply one variety of Galician-Portuguese, along with
       <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_Portuguese" title="Brazilian Portuguese">
        Brazilian Portuguese
       </a>
       ;
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Portuguese_in_Africa" title="Portuguese in Africa">
        African Portuguese
       </a>
       ; the Galician-Portuguese still spoken in Spanish Extremadura,
       <a href="/wiki/Fala_language" title="Fala language">
        Fala
       </a>
       ; and other dialects.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Political_implications">
        Political implications
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Galician_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Political implications">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       These contrasting attitudes have distinct political implications. Considering Galician as an independent language reduces contact with Portuguese culture, leaving Galician as a minor language with less capacity to counterbalance the influence of Spanish, the only official language between the 18th century and 1975. On the other hand, viewing Galician as a part of the Lusophony, while not denying its own characteristics (cf.
       <a href="/wiki/Swiss_German" title="Swiss German">
        Swiss German
       </a>
       ), shifts cultural influence from the Spanish domain to the Portuguese. Although it is difficult to clarify the political positions of those who favour one view or the other, the vindication of Galician as an independent language is generally associated with more conservative political thought linked to certain Spanish political and administrative structures. Some scholar authors describe the situation as properly a continuum, from the Galician variants of Portuguese in one extreme to the Spanish language in the other (which would represent the complete linguistic shift from Galician to Spanish); reintegrationist points of view are closer to the Portuguese extreme, and so-called isolationist ones would be closer to the Spanish one.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18">
        <a href="#cite_note-18">
         [18]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Geographic_distribution_and_legal_status">
        Geographic distribution and legal status
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Galician_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Geographic distribution and legal status">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       Galician is spoken by some three million people, including most of the population of
       <a href="/wiki/Galicia_(Spain)" title="Galicia (Spain)">
        Galicia
       </a>
       and the numerous Galician communities established elsewhere, in Spain (
       <a href="/wiki/Madrid" title="Madrid">
        Madrid
       </a>
       , Barcelona,
       <a href="/wiki/Biscay" title="Biscay">
        Biscay
       </a>
       ), in other European cities (
       <a href="/wiki/Andorra_la_Vella" title="Andorra la Vella">
        Andorra la Vella
       </a>
       , Geneva, London, Paris), and in the Americas (New York,
       <a href="/wiki/New_Jersey" title="New Jersey">
        New Jersey
       </a>
       , Buenos Aires, Cordoba/Argentina,
       <a href="/wiki/Montevideo" title="Montevideo">
        Montevideo
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Havana" title="Havana">
        Havana
       </a>
       , Caracas,
       <a href="/wiki/Mexico_City" title="Mexico City">
        Mexico City
       </a>
       , São Paulo,
       <a href="/wiki/Managua" title="Managua">
        Managua
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Guadalajara" title="Guadalajara">
        Guadalajara
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Veracruz_City" title="Veracruz City">
        Veracruz City
       </a>
       , Panama City).
      </p>
      <p>
       Galician is today official, together with the Spanish (Castilian) language, in the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Autonomous_community" title="Autonomous community">
        autonomous community
       </a>
       of Galicia, where it is recognized as the autochthonous language (
       <i>
        lingua propia
       </i>
       ), being the first language of the local administrations and governments
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2017)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       . It is supposedly by law to be taught bilingually, alongside Castilian, in both primary and secondary education. although the accomplishment of this law is allegedly doubted. It is also used at the three universities established in Galicia, having also the consideration of official language of the three institutions. Galician has also legal recognition in the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bierzo" title="Bierzo">
        Bierzo
       </a>
       region in
       <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Le%C3%B3n" title="Province of León">
        León
       </a>
       , and in four municipalities in
       <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Zamora" title="Province of Zamora">
        Zamora
       </a>
       . The other languages with official status elsewhere in Spain are
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">
        Castilian
       </a>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/Names_given_to_the_Spanish_language" title="Names given to the Spanish language">
        also called
        <i>
         Spanish
        </i>
       </a>
       ),
       <a href="/wiki/Catalan_language" title="Catalan language">
        Catalan
       </a>
       (or
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Valencian_language" title="Valencian language">
        Valencian
       </a>
       ),
       <a href="/wiki/Basque_language" title="Basque language">
        Basque
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aranese_language" title="Aranese language">
        Aranese
       </a>
       . Galician has also been accepted orally as
       <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">
        Portuguese
       </a>
       in the
       <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament" title="European Parliament">
        European Parliament
       </a>
       , having been used by some Galician representatives, among others:
       <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Posada" title="José Posada">
        José Posada
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Camilo_Nogueira" title="Camilo Nogueira">
        Camilo Nogueira
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Xos%C3%A9_Manuel_Beiras" title="Xosé Manuel Beiras">
        Xosé Manuel Beiras
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Controversy exists regarding the inclusion of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eonavian" title="Eonavian">
        Eonavian
       </a>
       (spoken in the western end of
       <a href="/wiki/Asturias" title="Asturias">
        Asturias
       </a>
       , bordering
       <a href="/wiki/Galicia_(Spain)" title="Galicia (Spain)">
        Galicia
       </a>
       ) into the Galician language, as it has some traits in common with
       <a href="/wiki/Asturian_language" title="Asturian language">
        Western Asturian or bable occidental
       </a>
       (spoken in the middle west of Asturias). There are those defending these linguistic varieties as
       <a href="/wiki/Dialect_continuum" title="Dialect continuum">
        dialects of transition
       </a>
       to the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Astur-Leonese_group" title="Astur-Leonese group">
        Astur-Leonese group
       </a>
       on the one hand, and those defending it as clearly Galician varieties on the other. The recent edition of the cartularies of Oscos in
       <a class="extiw" href="https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/Antiguo_concejo_de_Castropol" title="es:Antiguo concejo de Castropol">
        Eonavia
       </a>
       and cartularies of
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Obona&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Obona (page does not exist)">
        Obona
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Cornellana" title="Cornellana">
        Cornellana
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Corias" title="Corias">
        Corias
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Belmonte_de_Miranda" title="Belmonte de Miranda">
        Belmonte
       </a>
       in middle west of Asturias have shown a huge difference in the medieval speech between both banks of the Navia river.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">
        <a href="#cite_note-19">
         [19]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20">
        <a href="#cite_note-20">
         [20]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">
        <a href="#cite_note-21">
         [21]
        </a>
       </sup>
       An examination of the old documents of the Eonavian monastery of Oscos, written from the late 12th to early 14th century to 16th century, shows a clear identification of this language with the Galician-Portuguese linguistic group; while contemporary parchments elsewhere in Asturias are written in Castilian (i.e. Spanish).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">
        <a href="#cite_note-22">
         [22]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The two most important traits of those commonly used to tell apart Galician-Portuguese and Asturian-Leonese varieties are the preservation of the mid-open vowels
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /ɛ/
       </span>
       and
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /ɔ/
       </span>
       , which became diphthongs in Asturian-Leonese, and the loss of intervocalic
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /n/
       </span>
       , preserved in the latter language.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23">
        <a href="#cite_note-23">
         [23]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="History">
        History
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Galician_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: History">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:ForoBoBurgo.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="979" data-file-width="709" height="235" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/ForoBoBurgo.jpg/170px-ForoBoBurgo.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/ForoBoBurgo.jpg/255px-ForoBoBurgo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/ForoBoBurgo.jpg/340px-ForoBoBurgo.jpg 2x" width="170"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:ForoBoBurgo.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         One of the oldest legal charters written in Galician, the constitutional charter of the Bo Burgo (Good Burg) of
         <a href="/wiki/Castro_Caldelas" title="Castro Caldelas">
          Castro Caldelas
         </a>
         , 1228
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="quotebox pullquote" style="float: right; clear: right; margin: 0.5em 0 0.8em 1.4em; width:250px; padding: 10px; border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 88%; background-color: #F9F9F9;">
       <div class="" style="background-color: #F9F9F9; color: black; text-align: center; font-size: larger; font-weight: bold;">
        <i>
         Excerpt of medieval Galician poetry (with English translation)
        </i>
       </div>
       <div class="" style="position: relative; text-align: left;">
        <div>
         <div class="poem">
          <p>
           Porque no mundo mengou a verdade,
           <br/>
           punhei um dia de a ir buscar;
           <br/>
           e, u por ela fui nom preguntar,
           <br/>
           disserom todos: «Alhur la buscade,
           <br/>
           ca de tal guisa se foi a perder,
           <br/>
           que nom podemos en novas haver
           <br/>
           nem já nom anda na irmaindade.»
           <br/>
           <br/>
           Because in the world the truth has faded,
           <br/>
           I decided to go a-searching for it
           <br/>
           and wherever I went asking for it
           <br/>
           everybody said: 'Search elsewhere
           <br/>
           because truth is lost in such a way
           <br/>
           such as we can have no news of it
           <br/>
           nor is it around here anymore.'
          </p>
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
       <cite style="display: block; text-align: right;">
        <a href="/wiki/Airas_Nunes" title="Airas Nunes">
         Airas Nunes
        </a>
        (B 871, V 455. 13th century)
       </cite>
      </div>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Further information:
       <a href="/wiki/Galician-Portuguese" title="Galician-Portuguese">
        Galician-Portuguese
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Texto_-_Noia_-_Galiza.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1443" data-file-width="3500" height="70" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Texto_-_Noia_-_Galiza.jpg/170px-Texto_-_Noia_-_Galiza.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Texto_-_Noia_-_Galiza.jpg/255px-Texto_-_Noia_-_Galiza.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Texto_-_Noia_-_Galiza.jpg/340px-Texto_-_Noia_-_Galiza.jpg 2x" width="170"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Texto_-_Noia_-_Galiza.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Mediaeval Galician inscription in a 14th-century house, in
         <a href="/wiki/Noia" title="Noia">
          Noia
         </a>
         : "ESTAS CASAS MANDOU FAZER VASCO DA COSTA, ERA DE MCCCLXXVII"
         <i>
          These houses were ordered by Vasco da Costa,
          <a href="/wiki/Spanish_era" title="Spanish era">
           era
          </a>
          1377 (1339 AD)
         </i>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Latinate Galician charters from the 8th century onward show that the local written Latin was heavily influenced by local spoken Romance, yet is not until the 12th century that we find evidence for the identification of the local language as a language different from Latin itself.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">
        <a href="#cite_note-24">
         [24]
        </a>
       </sup>
       During this same 12th century we can find full Galician sentences being inadvertently used inside Latin texts, while its first reckoned use as a literary language dates to the last years of this same century.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25">
        <a href="#cite_note-25">
         [25]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26">
        <a href="#cite_note-26">
         [26]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The linguistic stage from the 13th to the 15th centuries is usually known as Galician-Portuguese (or
       <i>
        Old Portuguese
       </i>
       , or
       <i>
        Old Galician
       </i>
       ) as an acknowledgement of the cultural and linguistic unity of Galicia and Portugal during the Middle Ages, as the two linguistic varieties differed only in dialectal minor phenomena.
      </p>
      <p>
       This language flourished during the 13th and 14th centuries as a language of culture, developing
       <a href="/wiki/Galician-Portuguese_lyric" title="Galician-Portuguese lyric">
        a rich lyric tradition
       </a>
       of which some 2000 compositions (
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cantigas" title="Cantigas">
         cantigas
        </a>
       </i>
       , meaning 'songs') have been preserved—a few hundred even with their musical score—in a series of collections, and belonging to four main genres:
       <b>
        cantigas de amor
       </b>
       , love songs, where a man sings for his ladylove;
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Cantiga_de_amigo" title="Cantiga de amigo">
         cantigas de amigo
        </a>
       </i>
       , where a woman sings for her boyfriend;
       <b>
        cantigas de escarnio
       </b>
       , crude, taunting, and sexual songs of scorn;
       <b>
        cantigas de maldecir
       </b>
       , where the poet vents his spleen openly; and also the
       <a href="/wiki/Cantigas_de_Santa_Maria" title="Cantigas de Santa Maria">
        Cantigas de Santa María
       </a>
       , which are religious songs.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27">
        <a href="#cite_note-27">
         [27]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The oldest known document is the poem
       <i>
        Ora faz ost'o Senhor de Navarra
       </i>
       by Joam Soares de Paiva, written around 1200. The first non-literary documents in Galician-Portuguese date from the early 13th century, the Noticia de Torto (1211) and the Testamento of
       <a href="/wiki/Afonso_II_of_Portugal" title="Afonso II of Portugal">
        Afonso II of Portugal
       </a>
       (1214), both samples of medieval notarial prose.
      </p>
      <p>
       Its most notable patrons—themselves reputed authors—were king
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dom_Dinis" title="Dom Dinis">
        Dom Dinis
       </a>
       in Portugal, and king
       <a href="/wiki/Alfonso_X_of_Castile" title="Alfonso X of Castile">
        Alfonso X the Learned
       </a>
       in Galicia, Castile and León, who was a great promoter of both Galician and
       <a href="/wiki/Castilian_Spanish" title="Castilian Spanish">
        Castilian Spanish
       </a>
       languages. Not just the kings encouraged literary creation in Galician-Portuguese, but also the noble houses of Galicia and Portugal, as being an author or bringing reputed troubadours into one's home became a way of promoting social prestige; as a result many noblemen, businessmen and clergymen of the 13th and 14th centuries became notable authors, such as Paio Gomes Charinho, lord of
       <a href="/wiki/Rianxo" title="Rianxo">
        Rianxo
       </a>
       , and the aforementioned kings.
      </p>
      <p>
       Aside from the lyric genres, Galicia developed also a minor tradition on literary prose, most notably in translation of European popular series, as those dealing with
       <a href="/wiki/King_Arthur" title="King Arthur">
        king Arthur
       </a>
       written by
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chretien_de_Troyes" title="Chretien de Troyes">
        Chretien de Troyes
       </a>
       , or those based on the
       <a href="/wiki/Roman_de_Troie" title="Roman de Troie">
        war of Troy
       </a>
       , usually paid and commissioned by noblemen who desired to read those romances in their own language. Other genres include history books (either translation of Spanish ones, or original creations like the
       <i>
        Chronicle of St. Mary of Iria
       </i>
       , by Rui Vasques), religious books, legal studies, and a treaty on horse breeding.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28">
        <a href="#cite_note-28">
         [28]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Prose literary creation in Galician had stopped by the 16th century, when
       <a href="/wiki/Printing_press" title="Printing press">
        printing press
       </a>
       became popular; the first complete translation of the Bible was not printed until the 20th century.
      </p>
      <p>
       As for other written uses of Galician, legal charters (last wills, hirings, sales, constitutional charters, city council book of acts, guild constitutions, books of possessions, and any type of public or private contracts and inventories) written in Galicia are to be found from 1230 to 1530—the earliest one probably a document from the monastery of
       <a href="/wiki/Mel%C3%B3n" title="Melón">
        Melón
       </a>
       , dated in 1231
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29">
        <a href="#cite_note-29">
         [29]
        </a>
       </sup>
       —being Galician by far the most used language during the 13th, 14th and 15th centuries, in substitution of Latin.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Diglossia_and_influence_of_the_Castilian_language">
        Diglossia and influence of the Castilian language
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Galician_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Diglossia and influence of the Castilian language">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <table class="mbox-small" role="presentation" style="background-color:#f9f9f9;border:1px solid #aaa;color:#000;">
       <tr>
        <td class="mbox-image">
         <div class="center">
          <div class="floatnone">
           <img alt="" data-file-height="160" data-file-width="160" height="50" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg/50px-Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg/75px-Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg/100px-Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg.png 2x" width="50"/>
          </div>
         </div>
        </td>
        <td class="mbox-text plainlist" style="line-height:1.1em">
         <div class="haudio">
          <div style="padding:4px 0">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Santa_Maria.ogg" title="File:Santa Maria.ogg">
            "Santa Maria, strela do dia"
           </a>
          </div>
          <div>
           <div class="mediaContainer" style="width:220px">
            <audio class="kskin" controls="" data-durationhint="150.21333333333" data-mwprovider="wikimediacommons" data-mwtitle="Santa_Maria.ogg" data-startoffset="0" id="mwe_player_0" preload="none" style="width:220px">
             <source data-bandwidth="209168" data-height="0" data-shorttitle="MP3" data-title="MP3" data-transcodekey="mp3" data-width="0" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/1/13/Santa_Maria.ogg/Santa_Maria.ogg.mp3" type="audio/mpeg"/>
             <source data-bandwidth="217597" data-height="0" data-shorttitle="Ogg source" data-title="Original Ogg file (218 kbps)" data-width="0" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/1/13/Santa_Maria.ogg" type='audio/ogg; codecs="vorbis"'/>
            </audio>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="description" style="padding:2px 0 0 0">
           A 13th-century Galician-Portuguese
           <i>
            Cantiga
           </i>
          </div>
         </div>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td class="mbox-text" colspan="2" style="line-height:1.1em">
         <hr/>
         <span>
          <i>
           Problems playing this file? See
           <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Media_help" title="Wikipedia:Media help">
            media help
           </a>
           .
          </i>
         </span>
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <p>
       Galician-Portuguese lost its political unity when the
       <a href="/wiki/County_of_Portugal" title="County of Portugal">
        County of Portugal
       </a>
       obtained its independence from the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Leon" title="Kingdom of Leon">
        Kingdom of Leon
       </a>
       , a transition initiated in 1139 and completed in 1179, establishing the
       <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Portugal" title="Kingdom of Portugal">
        Kingdom of Portugal
       </a>
       . Meanwhile, the Kingdom of Galicia was united with the Kingdom of León, and later with the Kingdom of Castile, under kings of the
       <a href="/wiki/House_of_Burgundy" title="House of Burgundy">
        House of Burgundy
       </a>
       . The Galician and Portuguese standards of the language diverged over time, following independent evolutionary paths. Portuguese was the official language of the Portuguese chancellery, while Galician was the usual language not only of troubadours and peasants, but also of local noblemen and clergy, and of their officials, so forging and maintaining two slightly different standards.
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:13th-century_unknown_painters_-_Cantigas_de_Alfonso_el_Sabio_-_WGA16031.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="840" data-file-width="598" height="239" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/13th-century_unknown_painters_-_Cantigas_de_Alfonso_el_Sabio_-_WGA16031.jpg/170px-13th-century_unknown_painters_-_Cantigas_de_Alfonso_el_Sabio_-_WGA16031.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/13th-century_unknown_painters_-_Cantigas_de_Alfonso_el_Sabio_-_WGA16031.jpg/255px-13th-century_unknown_painters_-_Cantigas_de_Alfonso_el_Sabio_-_WGA16031.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/13th-century_unknown_painters_-_Cantigas_de_Alfonso_el_Sabio_-_WGA16031.jpg/340px-13th-century_unknown_painters_-_Cantigas_de_Alfonso_el_Sabio_-_WGA16031.jpg 2x" width="170"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:13th-century_unknown_painters_-_Cantigas_de_Alfonso_el_Sabio_-_WGA16031.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Cantigas_de_Santa_Maria" title="Cantigas de Santa Maria">
          Cantigas de Santa Maria
         </a>
         , 13th century
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       During the reign of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alfonso_X" title="Alfonso X">
        Alfonso X
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">
        Castilian Spanish
       </a>
       became the official language of the chancellery of the Kingdom of Castile. However, in Galicia and neighboring regions of Asturias and León in 1200–1500, the local languages remained the usual written languages in any type of document, either legal or narrative, public or private. Castilian was progressively introduced through Royal decrees and the edicts of foreign churchmen and officials. This led, from the late 15th century on, to the end of legal documents in Galician; the last ones were issued around 1530.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mariño_30-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Mariño-30">
         [30]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Also, from 1480 on, notaries of the
       <a href="/wiki/Crown_of_Castile" title="Crown of Castile">
        Crown of Castile
       </a>
       were required to obtain their licenses in
       <a href="/wiki/Toledo,_Spain" title="Toledo, Spain">
        Toledo
       </a>
       , where they had to prove their mastery of Spanish.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mariño_30-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Mariño-30">
         [30]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Galician_Johan_Tuorum.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1600" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Galician_Johan_Tuorum.jpg/220px-Galician_Johan_Tuorum.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Galician_Johan_Tuorum.jpg/330px-Galician_Johan_Tuorum.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Galician_Johan_Tuorum.jpg/440px-Galician_Johan_Tuorum.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Galician_Johan_Tuorum.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         14th-century inscription, in Galician language: 'ESTA : IMAGEE : HE : AQVI : POSTA : POR: ALMA : D(E) : I(O)HA(N) : TVORUM' 'This image is here in exposition for the soul of Joham Tuorum'.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       In spite of Galician being the most spoken language, during the 17th century the elites of the Kingdom began speaking Castilian, most notably in towns and cities. The linguistic situation in Galicia became one of
       <a href="/wiki/Diglossia" title="Diglossia">
        diglossia
       </a>
       , with Galician as the low variety and Spanish as the high one.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31">
        <a href="#cite_note-31">
         [31]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In reaction to the relegation of the autochthonous language, a series of literary and historical works (always written in Spanish) appeared in the 17th century through 19th century, meant to vindicate the history, language, people, and culture of Galicia.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32">
        <a href="#cite_note-32">
         [32]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The period from the 16th century to the early 19th century, when Galician had little literary—and no legal—use, is considered the dark age of Galician language. The Galician spoken and written then is usually referred to as
       <i>
        Middle Galician
       </i>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Middle_Galician">
        Middle Galician
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Galician_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Middle Galician">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mart%C3%ADn_Sarmiento.jpeg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1013" data-file-width="696" height="320" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Mart%C3%ADn_Sarmiento.jpeg/220px-Mart%C3%ADn_Sarmiento.jpeg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Mart%C3%ADn_Sarmiento.jpeg/330px-Mart%C3%ADn_Sarmiento.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Mart%C3%ADn_Sarmiento.jpeg/440px-Mart%C3%ADn_Sarmiento.jpeg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mart%C3%ADn_Sarmiento.jpeg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <i>
          Martín Sarmiento
         </i>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Middle Galician is known mostly through popular literature (songs, carols, proverbs, theatrical scripts, personal letters), but also through the frequent apparition of Galician interferences and personal and place names in local works and documents otherwise written in Spanish. Other important sources are a number of
       <a href="/wiki/Sonnet" title="Sonnet">
        sonnets
       </a>
       and other lyric poetry, as well as other literate productions, including the forgery of allegedly mediaeval scriptures or chronicles under diverse pretensions—usually to show the ancient nobility of the forger's family—being these writings elaborated in an archaic looking Galician which nevertheless couldn't conceal the state of the language during this period.
      </p>
      <p>
       Middle Galician is characterized by a series of phonetic processes which led to a further separation from Portuguese, and to the apparition of some of the more notorious dialectal features, among other phenomenons: emergence of the
       <i>
        gheada
       </i>
       or pronunciation of
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /ɡ/
       </span>
       as a pharyngeal fricative; denasalization of nasal vowels in most of Galicia, becoming oral vowels in the east, or a group formed by an oral vowels plus a nasal in the west; reduction of the sibilant system, with the confluence (except in the
       <i>
        Baixa Limia
       </i>
       region) of voiced and voiceless fricatives, followed by a process of de-affrication which led to different results in the west and in the east.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33">
        <a href="#cite_note-33">
         [33]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The most important author during this period of the language was the
       <a href="/wiki/Enlightenment_(spiritual)" title="Enlightenment (spiritual)">
        enlightened
       </a>
       scholar
       <a href="/wiki/Mart%C3%ADn_Sarmiento" title="Martín Sarmiento">
        Martín Sarmiento
       </a>
       , unconditional defender and the first researcher of Galician language (history, evolution, lexicon, etymology, onomastics). His
       <i>
        Elementos etimológicos segun el método de Euclides
       </i>
       (1766), written in Spanish but dealing with Galician, was in fact one of the first comprehensive studies on sound change and evolution of any European language.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34">
        <a href="#cite_note-34">
         [34]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span id="Rexurdimento_.28Renaissance.29">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Rexurdimento_(Renaissance)">
        Rexurdimento (Renaissance)
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Galician_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Rexurdimento (Renaissance)">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Eduardopondal.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="467" data-file-width="300" height="265" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Eduardopondal.jpg/170px-Eduardopondal.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Eduardopondal.jpg/255px-Eduardopondal.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/fc/Eduardopondal.jpg 2x" width="170"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Eduardopondal.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The 19th-century author,
         <a href="/wiki/Eduardo_Pondal" title="Eduardo Pondal">
          Eduardo Pondal
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       During the 19th century a thriving literature developed, in what was called the
       <i>
        Rexurdimento
       </i>
       (Resurgence), of the Galician language.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35">
        <a href="#cite_note-35">
         [35]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It was headed by three main authors:
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rosalia_de_Castro" title="Rosalia de Castro">
        Rosalia de Castro
       </a>
       , an intimist poet;
       <a href="/wiki/Eduardo_Pondal" title="Eduardo Pondal">
        Eduardo Pondal
       </a>
       , of nationalist ideology, who championed a Celtic revival; and
       <a href="/wiki/Manuel_Curros_Enr%C3%ADquez" title="Manuel Curros Enríquez">
        Manuel Curros Enríquez
       </a>
       , a liberal and anticlerical author whose ideas and proclamations were scandalous for part of the 19th-century society.
      </p>
      <p>
       An important landmark was the establishment of the
       <a href="/wiki/Seminario_de_Estudos_Galegos" title="Seminario de Estudos Galegos">
        Seminario de Estudos Galegos
       </a>
       in 1923, devoted to research and study of Galician culture. It was created by a group of students:
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Ferm%C3%ADn_Bouza_Brey&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Fermín Bouza Brey (page does not exist)">
        Fermín Bouza Brey
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Xos%C3%A9_Filgueira_Valverde" title="Xosé Filgueira Valverde">
        Xosé Filgueira Valverde
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Lois_Tob%C3%ADo_Fern%C3%A1ndez" title="Lois Tobío Fernández">
        Lois Tobío Fernández
       </a>
       , with the collaboration of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ricardo_Carvalho_Calero" title="Ricardo Carvalho Calero">
        Ricardo Carvalho Calero
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Ant%C3%B3n_Fraguas&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Antón Fraguas (page does not exist)">
        Antón Fraguas
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Xaqu%C3%ADn_Lorenzo_Fern%C3%A1ndez" title="Xaquín Lorenzo Fernández">
        Xaquín Lorenzo Fernández
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Following the victory of General
       <a href="/wiki/Francisco_Franco" title="Francisco Franco">
        Francisco Franco
       </a>
       in the
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Civil_War" title="Spanish Civil War">
        Spanish Civil War
       </a>
       , the written or public use of the Galician language was outlawed.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36">
        <a href="#cite_note-36">
         [36]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Percentage_of_Galician_speakers_(corrected).PNG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1054" data-file-width="1692" height="137" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Percentage_of_Galician_speakers_%28corrected%29.PNG/220px-Percentage_of_Galician_speakers_%28corrected%29.PNG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Percentage_of_Galician_speakers_%28corrected%29.PNG/330px-Percentage_of_Galician_speakers_%28corrected%29.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Percentage_of_Galician_speakers_%28corrected%29.PNG/440px-Percentage_of_Galician_speakers_%28corrected%29.PNG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Percentage_of_Galician_speakers_(corrected).PNG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Speakers of Galician as first language in 2001, Galician Institute of Statistics
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Galician_linguistic_areas.PNG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1308" data-file-width="1485" height="194" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Galician_linguistic_areas.PNG/220px-Galician_linguistic_areas.PNG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Galician_linguistic_areas.PNG/330px-Galician_linguistic_areas.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Galician_linguistic_areas.PNG/440px-Galician_linguistic_areas.PNG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Galician_linguistic_areas.PNG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Galician linguistic areas
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Galizaestremeira.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="624" data-file-width="641" height="214" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Galizaestremeira.png/220px-Galizaestremeira.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Galizaestremeira.png/330px-Galizaestremeira.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Galizaestremeira.png/440px-Galizaestremeira.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Galizaestremeira.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Galician-speaking areas outside Galicia (yellow)
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Publishing of Galician-language material revived on a small scale in the 1950s.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jm_37-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-jm-37">
         [37]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Galician_language_today">
        Galician language today
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Galician_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Galician language today">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       With the advent of democracy, Galician has been brought into the country's institutions, and it is now co-official with Spanish in Galicia.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jm_37-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-jm-37">
         [37]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Galician is taught in schools, and there is a public Galician-language television channel,
       <a href="/wiki/Televisi%C3%B3n_de_Galicia" title="Televisión de Galicia">
        Televisión de Galicia
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Today, the most common language for everyday use in the largest cities of Galicia is Spanish rather than Galician, as a result of this long process of
       <a href="/wiki/Language_shift" title="Language shift">
        language shift
       </a>
       . However, Galician is still the main language in rural areas.
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Royal_Galician_Academy" title="Royal Galician Academy">
        Royal Galician Academy
       </a>
       and other Galician institutions celebrate each 17 May as
       <a href="/wiki/Galician_Literature_Day" title="Galician Literature Day">
        Galician Literature Day
       </a>
       (
       <i>
        <span lang="gl">
         Día das Letras Galegas
        </span>
       </i>
       ), dedicated each year to a deceased Galician-language writer chosen by the academy.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Use_of_Galician_language">
        Use of Galician language
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Galician_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Use of Galician language">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Use of Galician splits by age, with over half of those over 45 indicating that Galician is their primary language, with lower numbers for the younger population. Those under 45 were more likely than those over 45 to answer that they never use Galician.
      </p>

      <p>

      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Dialects">
        Dialects
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Galician_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Dialects">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       Some authors are of the opinion that Galician possesses no real dialects.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38">
        <a href="#cite_note-38">
         [38]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Despite this, Galician local varieties are collected in three main
       <a href="/wiki/Dialect" title="Dialect">
        dialectal
       </a>
       blocks, each block comprising a series of areas, being local linguistic varieties that are all
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mutually_intelligible" title="Mutually intelligible">
        mutually intelligible
       </a>
       . Some of the main features which distinguish the three blocks are:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        The resolution of medieval
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nasalized_vowels" title="Nasalized vowels">
         nasalized vowels
        </a>
        and
        <a href="/wiki/Hiatus_(linguistics)" title="Hiatus (linguistics)">
         hiatus
        </a>
        : these sometimes turned into
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Diphthongs" title="Diphthongs">
         diphthongs
        </a>
        in the east, while in the center and west the vowels in the hiatus were sometimes assimilated. Later, in the eastern—except Ancarese Galician—and central blocks, the nasal trait was lost, while in the west the nasal trait usually developed into an implosive
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39">
         <a href="#cite_note-39">
          [39]
         </a>
        </sup>
        nasal consonant
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /ŋ/
        </span>
        . In general, these led to important dialectal variability in the inflection in genre and number of words ended in a nasal consonant. So, from medieval
        <i>
         irmão
        </i>
        'brother',
        <i>
         ladrões
        </i>
        'robbers',
        <i>
         irmãas
        </i>
        'sisters' we have eastern Galician
        <i>
         irmao
        </i>
        ,
        <i>
         ladrois
        </i>
        ,
        <i>
         irmás
        </i>
        ; central Galician
        <i>
         irmao
        </i>
        ,
        <i>
         ladrós
        </i>
        ,
        <i>
         irmás
        </i>
        ; western Galician
        <i>
         irmán
        </i>
        ,
        <i>
         ladróns
        </i>
        ,
        <i>
         irmáns
        </i>
        .
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40">
         <a href="#cite_note-40">
          [40]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        An exception to this rule is constituted by the hiatus in which the first vowel was a nasalized i or u. In those cases, a nasal, palatal
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /ɲ/
        </span>
        or velar
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /ŋ/
        </span>
        was usually inserted:
        <i>
         ũa
        </i>
        'a / one (fem.)' &gt;
        <i>
         unha
        </i>
        (Portuguese
        <i>
         uma
        </i>
        ), -
        <i>
         ina
        </i>
        &gt; -
        <i>
         ĩa
        </i>
        &gt; -
        <i>
         iña
        </i>
        (Portuguese -
        <i>
         inha
        </i>
        ). Nevertheless, in Ancarese and Asturian Galician, this process did not take place: A-G
        <i>
         vecía
        </i>
        , Ancarese
        <i>
         vecĩa
        </i>
        vs. standard
        <i>
         veciña
        </i>
        '(female) neighbor' (Port.
        <i>
         vizinha
        </i>
        ), A-G
        <i>
         úa
        </i>
        , Ancarese
        <i>
         ũa
        </i>
        vs. standard
        <i>
         unha
        </i>
        (Port. uma).
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <ul>
       <li>
        The resolution of hiatus formed by oral vowels had similar developments, most notably those derived from the loss of
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /l/
        </span>
        , which again had important consequences for the declension of words ending in
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /l/
        </span>
        . So, Medieval Galician
        <i>
         animaes
        </i>
        'animals' (sing.
        <i>
         animal
        </i>
        ); central and western Galician
        <i>
         animás
        </i>
        ; eastern Galician
        <i>
         animais
        </i>
        ; Asturian Galician
        <i>
         animales
        </i>
        (
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /l/
        </span>
        is preserved).
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41">
         <a href="#cite_note-41">
          [41]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        In the west,
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /ɡ/
        </span>
        is rendered as a fricative
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         [
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          <a href="/wiki/Voiceless_velar_fricative" title="Voiceless velar fricative">
           x
          </a>
         </span>
         ~
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          <a href="/wiki/Voiceless_pharyngeal_fricative" title="Voiceless pharyngeal fricative">
           ħ
          </a>
         </span>
         ~
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          <a href="/wiki/Voiceless_glottal_fricative" title="Voiceless glottal fricative">
           h
          </a>
         </span>
         ]
        </span>
        (
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Gheada" title="Gheada">
          gheada
         </a>
        </i>
        ), except after a nasal, where it can become a stop
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         [
         <a href="/wiki/Voiceless_velar_stop" title="Voiceless velar stop">
          k
         </a>
         ]
        </span>
        .
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42">
         <a href="#cite_note-42">
          [42]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        Stressed vowel
        <a href="/wiki/Metaphony_(Romance_languages)" title="Metaphony (Romance languages)">
         metaphony
        </a>
        is most notable in the west and center, while in the east it is unknown. It is triggered by a final
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /o/
        </span>
        , which tends to close
        <a href="/wiki/Open-mid_vowel" title="Open-mid vowel">
         open-mid vowels
        </a>
        , or by a final
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /a/
        </span>
        which tends to open
        <a href="/wiki/Close-mid_vowel" title="Close-mid vowel">
         close-mid
        </a>
        ones.
       </li>
       <li>
        There are three main
        <a href="/wiki/Sibilant" title="Sibilant">
         sibilant
        </a>
        systems, all derived from the medieval Galician one, which were richer and more complex:
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43">
         <a href="#cite_note-43">
          [43]
         </a>
        </sup>
        <ul>
         <li>
          The common one, extended in the eastern and center regions, presents an opposition
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           /ʃ/ – /s/ – /θ/
          </span>
          . In the westernmost parts of this area the opposition of
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           /s/
          </span>
          and
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           /θ/
          </span>
          is lost in postnuclear position, in the coda, both being produced
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           /s/
          </span>
          .
         </li>
         <li>
          In the coastal western areas the opposition is
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           /ʃ/ – /s/
          </span>
          ,
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           /s/
          </span>
          being produced in some regions as a laminal or in some others as an apical. Sometimes this system is even further reduced to just a single
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           /s/
          </span>
          . On the other hand, in some areas final
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           /s/
          </span>
          is produced as
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           /ʃ/
          </span>
          .
         </li>
         <li>
          In the Limia Baixa region an old six sibilant system is still preserved, with voiced/voiceless opposition:
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           /ʃ/ – /ʒ/
          </span>
          ;
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           /s̺/ – /z̺/
          </span>
          (apical) and
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           /s̻/ – /z̻/
          </span>
          (laminal).
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44">
           <a href="#cite_note-44">
            [44]
           </a>
          </sup>
         </li>
        </ul>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       Each dialectal area is then further defined by these and other more restricted traits or isoglosses:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <b>
         Eastern Galician
        </b>
        : Asturian area (
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eonavian" title="Eonavian">
         Eonavian
        </a>
        ), Ancares area, Zamora area and Central-Eastern area.
       </li>
       <li>
        <b>
         Central Galician
        </b>
        : Mindoniense area, Lucu-auriense area, Central Transitional area, and Eastern Transitional area.
       </li>
       <li>
        <b>
         Western Galician
        </b>
        : Bergantiños area, Fisterra area, Pontevedra area and Lower Limia area.
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       Standard Galician is usually based on Central Galician characteristics, but it also incorporates western and eastern traits and features.
      </p>
